I soaked the plates briefly in hot water to loosen the plastic, then using an emory board to grab an edge of the blue plastic I was able to pull it away from the edge of the disk and remove it smoothly in one piece. The plates were then carefully dried. Without the hot water soak and emory board I would have shredded my fingers trying to remove that blue plastic. Be careful handling these plates they really are sharp but the designs are great.

  244. I ordered these before reading the reviews. After reading the reviews I was worried about the quality of these plates. I tried them out, and I'm quite pleased with them. 1) Yes, getting the protective blue film off is not the easiest thing in the world, but with patience it does come off. Don't just tear at it. Peel it up from the edge carefully. Once you have enough to get a grip on, peel it off the rest slowly. It will come off. 2) One of the other reviewers went commented about how she had tiny hands and how the whole nail designs were just too small to cover her whole finger nails. I have regular sized hands and naturally long nails. Most of the whole nail designs are plenty big to cover my nails. Only some of them are too short to cover end to end on my nails. My longest nails are about 3/4 inch long right now. 3) As some other reviewers have stated, the edges are SHARP. After comparing the SHANY plates to my Konad plates, it isn't because the SHANY plates are any thinner. The problem is that the edges of each plate were never buffed smooth after they were punched out of the sheet of metal. I think I'm going to \\"fix\\" this by putting a large label on the back and cutting around the edge of the plate. That should cover the sharp edges and prevent any slicing of fingers. A couple other notes. I think these are a great value for the money. Lots of nice designs. I'm really liking the french manicure designs. MUCH less expensive than the Konad plates. The edges are sharp enough that without the blue film on the plates, I don't want to stack the plates as I'm afraid the sharp edges of the plate on top will scratch the surface of the plate below.

  294. I was so happy when these arrived; cute designs, great packaging, easy to use (with the Konad stamper and scraper I also bought, based on the reviews). Some of the designs I will probably never use, but there are plenty to like in this pack, and at a good price (the Konad stamping plates by comparison cost an arm and a leg). My only complaint here is that some of the square whole-nail designs are not large enough to cover my whole thumb nail in one go.<br /><br />To use these stamping plates:<br />1. Have a stamper and scraper ready.<br />2. Remove the blue film on the stamping plate.<br />3. Place the plate on a paper towel or other surface you can clean the nail polish off of.<br />4. Paint the design you want with the desired nail polish color.<br />5. Working quickly before it dries, drag the scraper across the design to remove the excess polish and let the excess wipe off on the paper towel. The remaining image should be crisp.<br />6. Carefully roll the stamper across the design to pick it up.<br />7. This is the tricky part; press the corner of the design gently onto your nail and, also gently, roll the stamper across the surface of the nail to deposit the whole design. This part may take some practice.<br /><br />For some of the larger images, I have had trouble getting them to deposit smoothly across the nail, so I am going to try making some &#34;nail stickers&#34; with them. For nail stickers, I paint some clear polish on some plastic, stamp the design on top, and then peel off the polish to make a &#34;sticker&#34; that I can apply to my nail. I haven't tried this yet, so I can't say how well this works, but might be worth a shot if you are having difficulties. Good luck!

  490. I absolutely love these plates. I have been wanting to do stamping for quite a while, but couldn't justify paying the price other companies were asking for just one single plate. So, when I came across these I jumped at the chance.<br /><br />After a lot of trial and error, and a bit of research, I have to say they work perfectly! I was skeptical at first, because I was just using my own nail polish to do the stamping. I read reviews, checked out the Shany website, etc. What I found out was I was using the wrong kind of polish. They make polish specifically for stamping, but if you insist on using your own it can't be brand new, thin, nail polish. It needs to be a thicker brand.<br /><br />So, after trying again with some old nail polish that I don't use, because it became a little too thick, the plates worked perfectly. Also, I read that you can rough up the little stamper with an emery board first, then cleanse it with some polish remover and that helps too. It really does!!! So, for those that have bought these and not found them to work perfectly, just keep practicing. Do some research, and you'll get the hang of it.<br /><br />The plates themselves were in perfect condition when I got them. All the images stamp very well, and I had no duplicates in the box. One more thing I forgot to mention, and also found out on trial and error, when you scrape the excess polish be sure to do it in different directions. Depending on the actual image that does make a difference. A couple of them I couldn't get to stamp right, so then I scraped the excess polish the other way and it stamped perfectly every time.<br /><br />Now I just need more different colors of polish. ^_^

I understand that sometimes big operations can go pear shaped and take much longer to fix small problems when it comes to a design error. The only reason I am not giving this a 1 star rating is that I can still use 18 of the plates fairly well, and I'm remaining hopeful that in the future SHANY will send me the replacement set for the mis-etched plates I did receive and I can come back and change this review.
